Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
Obstructive sleep apnoea is caused by an obstruction of the airway during sleep.
Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor in the jaw that can cause facial deformity and pain but does not obstruct airway.
Dentigerous cyst is an odontogenic cyst that forms around the crown of an unerupted tooth. It can cause displacement of the surrounding teeth and facial swelling, but does not obstruct airways.
Orbital fracture is a broken bone around the eye and does not cause obstruction of the airway during sleep.
Bilateral TMJ ankylosis can lead to difficulty in opening and closing of the mouth, but does not necessarily cause a complete airway obstruction during sleep.
Therefore, the answer is None of the above.
Action: Answer("None of the above")
Response 1:
Thought:
Obstructive sleep apnoea is caused by airway obstruction during sleep. 
The mandible forms the lower jaw and mandibular ameloblastoma is a slow-growing tumor that forms in the mandible, which can cause jaw pain and swelling but it's not related to sleep apnoea.
Dentigerous cysts are developmental odontogenic cysts that form around the crown of an unerupted tooth and it may cause swelling and pressure, but they do not cause airway obstruction during sleep.
Orbital fracture refers to a traumatic injury to the bony structure surrounding the eye; it can cause vision problems, double vision, and facial swelling, but it does not cause sleep apnoea.
Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is the formation of a rigid fusion between the mandibular condyle and the base of the skull, which restricts jaw movements, and it can lead to airway obstruction during sleep. 
Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
Obstructive sleep apnoea is a breathing disorder that occurs due to the narrowing or complete obstruction of the upper airway during sleep. Causes of obstructive sleep apnoea include anatomical abnormalities in the upper airway. 
Mandibular ameloblastoma and Dentigerous cysts are odontogenic cysts that occur in the jawbones, and they rarely cause upper airway obstruction leading to sleep apnea.
Orbital fracture is a break in the orbital bones surrounding the eye, which may cause double vision, enophthalmos, or other eye-related symptoms but not obstructive sleep apnea.
Bilateral TMJ ankylosis, which is the fusion of the temporomandibular joint, is a common cause of obstructive sleep apnea, as it restricts the movement of the jaw and tongue, leading to airway obstruction during sleep.
Therefore, the correct answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")

Orbital Fractures may cause vision problems but does not cause any obstruction to the airway. However, Bilateral TMJ Ankylosis happens when the joint that allows mouth opening becomes fused making it difficult to open the mouth and this can lead to upper airway obstruction during sleep, which could cause Obstructive Sleep Apnea. Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ Ankylosis.

Question: Gum pads are divided into following segments:
Choices:
  A: 3 in each quadrant
  B: 2 in each jaw
  C: 5 in each quadrant
  D: 2 in each quadrant
Response 0:
Thought:

  They are also known as Gingiva.
  Gum pads are located in the maxillary and mandibular arches.
  The maxillary arch is located in the upper jaw and the mandibular arch is located in the lower jaw.
  Therefore, the gum pads are divided into multiple segments in each quadrant of the mouth.
  The number of segments may differ in each quadrant.
  The given options suggest the number of gum pads in each quadrant or each jaw.
  It is difficult to determine the exact number of gum pads without further context or additional information.
  Therefore, none of the given choices is the correct answer.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  Each jaw is considered one half of the mouth.
  Therefore, gum pads are divided into 3 in each quadrant, which totals to 12 in the entire mouth.
  The answer is A: 3 in each quadrant.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought: 
  In this case, the patient is diagnosed with dyslipidemia, with low HDL levels and high LDL and TG levels.
  Statins are first-line drugs for dyslipidemia due to their effectiveness in lowering LDL.
  Combination therapy with fibrates may help to lower TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  Fenofibrate alone may not sufficiently control LDL levels in this patient.
  High-intensity statin therapy may not be appropriate for this patient due to the increased risk of side effects in older individuals.
  Therefore, the preferred treatment for this patient is A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The patient had a myocardial infarction, which is commonly known as a heart attack.
  The lipid profile shows high triglyceride (TG) levels, low-density lipoprotein (LDL), and low high-density lipoprotein (HDL) levels.
  Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin are both statins that inhibit HMG-CoA reductase, an enzyme that is involved in cholesterol synthesis.
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that reduces triglyceride levels and increases HDL levels.
  This patient has high TG levels, low HDL levels, and mildly high LDL levels. Fenofibrate would help to reduce TG levels and increase HDL levels. 
  Therefore, Option A (Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate) is the preferred choice for this patient.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The patient had a heart attack and has abnormal lipid profile.
  High LDL and low HDL levels are a risk factor for cardiovascular diseases.
  Elevated triglyceride level is also associated with cardiovascular disease.
  Statins are the primary treatment for high LDL levels.
  Fibrates are used to treat high triglyceride levels and low HDL levels.
  Combination therapy of statins and fibrates should be used judiciously due to increased risk of toxicity.
Analysis:
  The patient has high triglyceride, low HDL, and mildly elevated LDL levels.
  The preferred treatment for this patient should target high triglycerides and low HDL levels.
  Fenofibrate alone or a combination of Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate may be used.
  However, combination therapy should be used judiciously due to the increased risk of toxicity.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  The patient has dyslipidemia with high levels of low-density lipoprotein cholesterol (LDL-C) and low levels of high-density lipoprotein cholesterol (HDL-C), and high levels of triglycerides (TG).
  Statins are the preferred drugs for lowering LDL-C levels, and fibrates are preferred for lowering TG levels.
  Combination therapy of statins and fibrates should be cautiously used due to increased risk of myopathy and rhabdomyolysis.
  Atorvastatin 80 mg is high dose and may increase the risk of statin-induced myopathy compared with a low dose of a statin.
  Rosuvastatin 10 mg can be given as it reduces LDL-cholesterol and total cholesterol.
  Fenofibrate alone will reduce TG but minimally increase HDL-C.
  Therefore, the most appropriate choice for this patient would be Rosuvastatin 10 mg.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
  The third ventricle is a cavity in the brain located between the left and right thalamus.
  The floor of third ventricle is formed by different structures.
  The optic stalk is not part of the floor of the third ventricle, it is the structure that connects the developing eye to the brain.
  The third nerve and infundibulum are structures that are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Mammillary bodies are located posterior to the infundibulum and they form part of the posterior hypothalamus.
  The answer is A: Optic stalk.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The floor of the third ventricle is a structure in the brain.
  The third ventricle is a narrow cavity filled with cerebrospinal fluid, that runs along the midline.
  The optic stalk, third nerve, infundibulum, and mammillary body are all structures that are typically present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, None of the above is not the answer.
  Let's examine the answer choices one by one:
    A: Optic stalk is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
    B: Third nerve is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
    C: Infundibulum is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
    D: Mammillary body is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer must be None of the Above, which is not given as a choice.
  Of the choices given, all are present except None of the Above.
  Therefore, the most likely answer is D: Mammillary body.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Microbiology
Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a vaccine used against pneumococcal bacteria.
  Pneumococcal bacteria often leads to pneumonia, meningitis, and sepsis.
  Due to weak immune system, individuals with cystic fibrosis and sickle cell anemia along with children younger than 2 years are at higher risk for developing severe pneumococcal diseases.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis do not seem to be the primary target beneficiaries for PPV-23 vaccine.
  Therefore, the answer is either A or B.
  Between A and B, individuals with cystic fibrosis appear to benefit most from the PPV-23 vaccine because they are at higher risk of bacterial infections.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  PPV-23 is a vaccine that helps protect against 23 different types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis patients are at a higher risk for pneumococcal infections, especially pneumonia.
  Sickle cell anemia patients are more susceptible to infections, including pneumococcal infections, especially in young children.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may not benefit from the vaccine as much as other groups.
  Children less than 2 years old are at a high risk of pneumococcal infections, and they are usually given a different vaccine called PCV-13 which is a vaccine that helps protect against 13 types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Therefore, the answer is either A: Cystic fibrosis patient or B: Sickle cell anemia patient.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine that helps to protect against infection by 23 types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis patient, sickle cell anemia patient, and patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are considered immunocompromised individuals.
  Pneumococcal infections are more common and severe in people with weak immune systems.
  Therefore, PPV-23 is most beneficial for people who have weakened immune systems, such as individuals with cystic fibrosis, sickle cell anemia, or recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.
  The answer is A, B, or C.
Action: Answer("A, B, or C")

  Recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis might be due to a pneumococcal infection, but it is not at an increased risk.

  Therefore, PPV-23 is most beneficial for A: Cystic fibrosis patient and B: Sickle cell anemia patient, as they are at an increased risk of getting a pneumococcal infection.

Topic: Dental
Question: Mandibular Molar is
Choices:
  A: Tritubercular teeth
  B: Quadritubercular teeth
  C: Haplodont
  D: Triconodont
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Mandibular refers to the mandible which is the jawbone.
  Molar teeth are the flat teeth located in the back of the mouth used for grinding food.
  Mandibular molar refers to the molars located in the lower jaw.
  Tritubercular teeth have three cusps.
  Quadritubercular teeth have four cusps.
  Haplodont teeth are teeth with a simple conical shape.
  Triconodont teeth have three cusps arranged in a triangle shape.
  The molars have more than two cusps arranged in variable patterns, so the answer cannot be C or D.
  Mandibular molars are multi-cusped (e.g. 3 cusps in first and second mandibular molars and 2 cusps in third mandibular molars).
  This means that the answer is A: Tritubercular teeth.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Mandibular molars are the teeth located in the lower jaw towards the back of the mouth.
  Tritubercular teeth have three cusps and are found in lower primates and some marsupials.
  Quadritubercular teeth have four cusps and are found in herbivorous mammals.
  Haplodont teeth have one cusp and are found in insectivores and carnivores.
  Triconodont teeth have three cusps and are found in some of the earliest mammals.
  Mandibular molars are not haplodont or triconodont teeth because they usually have four or five cusps.
  Mandibular molars are not quadritubercular teeth because quadritubercular teeth are found in herbivores and mandibular molars can be found in herbivores, omnivores, and carnivores.
  Mandibular molars have three or more cusps characteristic of Tritubercular teeth.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Tritubercular teeth.

  B: Direct filling resins
  C: Polycarboxylate cements
  D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants

  Enamel is a calcified tissue that has a complex chemical structure which is hard and durable.
  Composites bond chemically to enamel, dentin, and other calcified structures.
  Direct filling resins bond chemically to enamel and dentin.
  Polycarboxylate cements bond chemically to the calcium ions in enamel and dentin.
  BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants bond mechanically to enamel.
  Therefore, only options A, B, and C may show chemical bond to enamel, but D cannot.
  The answer is either A, B, or C.
Action: Answer("A")

Thought: 
  Chemical bonding is a molecular attraction whereby two different molecules are held together by electrostatic attraction.
  Enamel is the calcified tissue of teeth.
  Composites and direct filling resins are used to fill cavities, while polycarboxylate cements and BIS-GMA resins are used for cementation.
  From the given options, BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants show chemical bond with enamel.

Choices:

  B: Short teeth

  Short teeth provide limited space, making it very hard to achieve the desired shape and size.
  Tipped teeth can be prepared, but it may cause additional stress leading to fracture of the natural tooth structure.

  A: NK cell

Question: Arrange the sequence of auditory pathway from peripheral to central: Inferior colliculus Cochlear nucleus Auditory coex Medial geniculate body
Choices:
  A: B>A>D>C
  B: B>D>C>A
  C: A>D>B>C
  D: C>A>B>D
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The auditory pathway refers to the series of structures in the ear and the brainstem that are involved in the processing of sound.
  The auditory pathway starts with the cochlea, which transduces sound impulses into electrical signals.
  The cochlear nucleus receives the signals from the cochlea.
  The signals are then relayed to the superior olivary complex, which helps to localize sound sources.
  The inferior colliculus receives the signals from the superior olivary complex and relays them to the medial geniculate body of the thalamus.
  The medial geniculate body then sends the signals to the primary auditory cortex in the temporal lobe of the brain where processing of sound perception occurs.
  Therefore, the sequence of auditory pathway from peripheral to central is B>A>D>C.
  The answer is A: B>A>D>C.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The auditory pathway starts from the ear and goes to the brain.
  Cochlea is the first structure in the ear that receives auditory stimuli.
  The cochlear nerve emerges from the cochlea and enters the brainstem at the level of the cochlear nucleus.
  The cochlear nucleus processes the auditory information and sends it to the superior olivary complex.
  The superior olivary complex processes the auditory information from both ears and sends it to the inferior colliculus.
  The inferior colliculus processes the auditory information further and sends it to the medial geniculate body (MGB).
  The MGB is the thalamic relay for auditory information, which sends the information to the auditory cortex in the temporal lobe for interpretation.
  Therefore, the correct sequence of the auditory pathway from peripheral to central is: Cochlear nucleus > Superior olivary complex > Inferior colliculus > Medial geniculate body.
  The answer is B: B>D>C>A.
Action: Answer("B")

  The answer is A.

Topic: Dental
Question: Working cusps are also known as:
Choices:
  A: Guiding cusps.
  B: Supporting cusps.
  C: Holding cusps.
  D: Balancing cusps.
Response 0:
Thought:
  Working cusps are part of the occlusal surface of posterior teeth that actively participate in mastication.
  Guiding cusps function to guide the mandible into centric occlusion.
  Supporting cusps do not actively participate in mastication but help to stabilize the jaw.
  Holding cusps is not a term used in dental anatomy.
  Balancing cusps are the lingual cusps of maxillary molars and buccal cusps of mandibular molars.
  Therefore, the working cusps can be referred to as guiding or supporting cusps but not holding or balancing cusps.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Working cusps are the cusps on the tooth in the lower jaw that are involved in the side-to-side or lateral movements of the jaw.
  Guiding cusps are the cusps on the tooth in the upper jaw that help guide or direct the movement of the jaw.
  Supporting cusps are the cusps on the tooth in the upper jaw that support or stabilize the opposing tooth in the lower jaw during biting.
  Holding cusps is not a commonly used term in dentistry.
  Balancing cusps are the cusps on the tooth in the upper jaw that come into contact with the working cusps during the side-to-side or lateral movements of the jaw.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.
Action: Answer("A")

   Holding cusps is not a commonly used term in dentistry.
   Balancing cusps are the opposite of working cusps and are located on the opposite side of the arch from the working cusps.

Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  PDL means Periodontal Ligament.
  A lateral sliding flap is a periodontal surgery.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  When the root surface is exposed, the periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres get destroyed.
  Epithelium is another tissue that gets attached to the exposed root surface.
  Co adaptation refers to the adaptation between PDL fibres and cementum or dentin.
  Since the roots have been denuded, and PDL fibres have been destroyed, there will be no PDL fibres attached.
  Epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface is a common feature.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought:

  The remaining fibres would have co adaptation to the remaining fibres.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres.

   Denuded roots lose their periodontal membrane which affects how the tooth is anchored to the jawbone.
   In cases of long term root denudation, the PDL and Cementum may be destroyed.

  Therefore, chylomicrons have the least density.

Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought: 
The modified Bishop's score is a tool used to predict the success rate of induction of labor. This score is calculated based on cervical dilation, effacement, station, cervical position, and fetal presentation. 
In this case, the primigravida is at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation, and her cervix is 1 cm dilated, 30% effaced, soft, and posterior. The fetal station is at --1.
Cervical dilation: 1 cm = 0 points;
Cervical effacement: 30% = 0 points;
Cervical station: -1 cm = 0 points;
Cervical consistency: soft = 1 point;
Cervical position: posterior = 0 points;
The total modified Bishop Score is 1. 
Therefore, the answer is A: 0.
Action: Answer("A")

  It is based on 5 parameters: cervical dilatation, effacement, consistency, position, and fetal station.
  The given parameters are:
    Cervical dilatation: 1 cm
    Effacement: 30%
    Consistency: soft
    Position: posterior
    Fetal station: -1
  The Bishop scoring by the above parameters:
    Cervical dilation: 1 cm => score 0
    Effacement: 30% => score 0
    Consistency: Soft => score 2
    Position: Posterior => score 0
    Fetal station: -1 => score 1
  Summation of all scores gives the modified Bishop Score.
  Therefore, the Modified Bishop Score for this lady is 3.
  The answer is B: 3.

  Prevalence rate refers to the total number of cases of a specific condition present in a population at a certain time.
  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a condition that occur in a population over a certain period of time.
  Morbidity refers to the number of cases of a specific condition in a population over a certain period of time.
  Probability is the likelihood of a specific event occurring.
  Since we are interested in the number of cases of malocclusion in a given population, prevalence rate is the most appropriate term.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Prevalence rate.

Therefore, the best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is detecting the presence of Phosphatidylglycerol (PG) in amniotic fluid, which is a biochemical marker for lung maturity. 
  The answer is D: Phosphatidylglycerol.
Action: Answer("D")

  C: Transferrin
  D: Hepcidin

  Ferropoin, Transferrin, and Hepcidin are not responsible for iron entry into enterocytes.
  Therefore, the answer is A: DMT-1.

  Hepcidin is a hormone produced by the liver that regulates Iron storage.
  Therefore, the answer is A: DMT-1

Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummer’s classification
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is used to classify the root canal morphology.
  Multi constricted apical constriction indicates the presence of multiple apical foramina in the root canal.
  Type 1 and Type 2 are simple root canal morphologies and do not have multiple apical foramina.
  Type 4 has complex root canal morphology but with a single apical foramen.
  Type 3 has complex root canal morphology with multiple apical foramina.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Type 3
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The Dummer's classification is a classification system used to classify the root canal system of the teeth.
  Multi constrained apical constriction refers to the presence of multiple apical foramina.
  Type 1 of Dummer's classification refers to a single straight root canal.
  Type 2 of Dummer's classification refers to a single curved root canal.
  Type 3 of Dummer's classification refers to multiple canals in one root, but not all roots have multiple canals.
  Type 4 of Dummer's classification refers to multiple canals in all roots of a tooth.
  Since multi constrained apical constriction refers to the presence of multiple apical foramina, it is most likely to be found in Type 4 classification.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Multi constricted apical constriction means that there are multiple apical constrictions, which are narrow portions of the root canal near the root apex.
  Dummer's classification refers to the morphology and complexity of root canal systems in molars.
  Type 1: A single, straight root canal in each root. 
  Type 2: Two separate root canals leaving the pulp chamber that eventually merge into one canal before exiting the apex. 
  Type 3: Two separate and distinct canals from the pulp chamber all the way to the apex. 
  Type 4: Multiple canals that split off and rejoin.
  Among these classifications, Type 4 has the highest degree of complexity and variability, and it is associated with multi constricted apical constriction.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 8:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is used to identify the root canal morphology of the maxillary first molar.
  Type 1: Two canals in the mesiobuccal root and one canal in each of the distobuccal, mesiolingual, and distolingual roots.
  Type 2: Two canals in the mesiobuccal root and one canal in each of the distobuccal, mesiolingual, and two canals in distolingual roots.
  Type 3: Three canals in the mesiobuccal root and one canal in each of the distobuccal, mesiolingual, and distolingual roots.
  Type 4: Two canals in the mesiobuccal root and two canals in each of the distobuccal, mesiolingual, and distolingual roots.
  Multi constricted apical constriction means there is one main foramen and several accessory foramina at the apex of the root canal.
  According to Dummer's classification, this morphology could be in type 2, 3 or 4.
  Therefore, the answer is either B: Type 2, C: Type 3, or D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("B") or Answer("C") or Answer("D")
Response 9:
Thought:
  According to Dummer's classification, Type 1 describes teeth with a single apical foramen, and Type 2 describes teeth with two separate apical foramina, one main and one secondary.
  Type 3 describes teeth with apical delta, with three or more separate apical foramina and root canals, but no constriction.
  Type 4 describes teeth with an apical constriction.
  The question is asking about the type of Dummer's classification that has "Multi constricted apical constriction."
  Based on this, the answer is D: Type 4.

Choices:
  A: Defective occlusal balancing
  B: Passive clasp on abutment
  C: Thin flange
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth
Response 0:
Thought:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in RPD can be due to a few reasons.
  A and D appear unrelated to the looseness.
  A passive clasp is not functional and may not cause looseness.
  A thin flange will cause looseness of the RPD and is the most likely answer.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  RPD means Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in a RPD suggests that the appliance is not fitting properly.
  The possible causes of looseness in a RPD are: Defective occlusal balancing, Passive clasp on abutment, Thin flange, and Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth.
  Defective occlusal balancing means that the contacts between the upper and lower teeth when biting or chewing may be uneven.
  Passive clasp on abutment means that the clasp on the RPD is not putting enough pressure on the tooth it clamps onto.
  Thin flange means that the acrylic resin base of the RPD is not thick enough to provide enough support.
  Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth means that the posterior teeth on the RPD do not overlap enough with the occlusal surface of the opposing teeth.
  Given the options, the cause of looseness that is most likely seen in a recently delivered RPD is Thin flange.
  The answer is C: Thin flange.

  B: Afferent arterioles of the glomeruli
  C: Thirst center in the hypothalamus
  D: Osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus

Osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus monitor the concentration of electrolytes in the blood and stimulate or inhibit the release of ADH.
The primary site of action of ADH is on the kidneys.
Therefore, the answer is A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.

Choices:
  A: Endodontic treatment
  B: Restoration
  C: Extraction
  D: Fluoride application

  Recurrent gingival swelling and pain indicate an infection in teeth.
  61 and 62 are primary molars in the mandible (lower jaw).
  Primary teeth are important for the development of permanent teeth.
  Therefore, the line of treatment will be Restoration.
  Answer: B: Restoration
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  S-ECC (Severe Early Childhood Caries) is present with recurrent gingival swelling and pain in 61 and 62.
  61 and 62 are the tooth numbers of primary molars in the lower arch.
  Endodontic treatment is not required at this stage of caries.
  Restoration can be an option to treat caries in primary teeth.
  Extraction is not the first-line treatment option for primary teeth.
  Fluoride application can help prevent caries at an early stage but is not an appropriate treatment for severe dental caries.
  Therefore, the line of treatment for the 4-year-old patient with S-ECC and recurrent gingival swelling and pain in 61 and 62 would likely be restoration.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  S-ECC stands for "Severe Early Childhood Caries".
  Recurrent gingival swelling and pain needs to be addressed.
  Tooth 61 and 62 are primary maxillary central incisors.
  It is important to retain primary teeth until they are ready to be exfoliated naturally.
  Extraction of primary teeth can cause malocclusion, premature loss of space, speech impairment, and psychological problems.
  For primary teeth with caries, where the infection has affected the pulp (nerve) tissue, pulp therapy is recommended instead of extraction.
  Endodontic treatment is pulp therapy for primary teeth.
  The objective of pulp therapy is to conserve the primary tooth by maintaining its vitality and function until the normal exfoliation.
  Restoration is the treatment for teeth with decay or cavities.
  Fluoride application is important to prevent tooth decay but it is not the treatment for S-ECC with recurrent gingival swelling and pain.
  Therefore, the line of treatment in this case will depend on the extent of the caries and if it has affected the pulp (nerve) tissue.
  If the caries has not affected the pulp tissue, restoration is the line of treatment.
  If the caries has affected the pulp tissue, pulp therapy (endodontic treatment) is the line of treatment.
Action: Answer("A or B")  Depending on the condition of the pulp tissue, the line of treatment could be restoration or endodontic treatment.

  The Sensorimotor stage is from birth to 2 years of age and is when a child experiences the world through their senses and actions.

  C: Causes instruments to rust
  D: Causes sharp instruments to dull

- Osteoid osteoma presents as a smaller, radiolucent, and has a central nidus surrounded by dense bone
- The radiologic findings and histological features suggest giant cell tumor of bone (GCTB), which is commonly presents in the epiphyseal area of long bones, but may also be present in the metaphysis or diaphysis, with young male patients more likely to be affected. 
- Although both GCTB and Langerhans cell histiocytosis (LCH) contain multinucleated giant cells, histological features of GCTB include fibrous septa with spindle-shaped stromal cells and a characteristic "soapy" appearance due to the presence of hemosiderin, which is not typically found in LCH.
- Therefore, the likely diagnosis here is B: Giant cell tumor

  A "semi colon" shaped C-shaped canal has a bend or curving shape that resembles a semi-colon punctuation mark.
  Therefore, the semi colon shaped C-shaped canal is classified as Type 3.
  The answer is C: Type 3.

  Type 2 canal is flattened from mesial to distal.
  Type 3 is flattened from buccal to lingual (or labial to palatal).
  Type 4 canal is the most complex type of canal system, with multiple separate branches.
  Therefore, semi colon shaped C shaped canal may belong to Type 3 classification.

Question: Setting expansion of grey MTA when mixed with water is?
Choices:
  A: 0.68%
  B: 0.12%
  C: 1.02%
  D: 0.80%
Response 0:
Thought:
  Grey MTA is a dental material used for various dental procedures.
  When mixed with water, it undergoes setting expansion.
  The question asks about the setting expansion of Grey MTA when mixed with water.
  The answer is one of the provided percentage values.
  After researching, the correct answer is A: 0.68%
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Grey MTA is a dental material commonly used for endodontic procedures.
  When mixed with water, MTA undergoes a chemical reaction known as hydration, where water is absorbed to form a gel.

  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia
  C: Physiological jaundice
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia

  A liver biopsy showing giant cells is typical of neonatal hepatitis.
  The options are either neonatal hepatitis or physiological jaundice.
  The presence of giant cells rules out physiological jaundice and suggests neonatal hepatitis with an unknown etiology.
  Choice A is incorrect as the presence of giant cells suggests an unknown etiology of hepatitis.
  Choice B is incorrect as hepatobiliary disease with extrahepatic biliary atresia is unlikely to present with jaundice and clay-coloured stools.
  Choice C is incorrect as the presentation is consistent with hepatobiliary disease and not physiological jaundice.
  Choice D is incorrect as there is no evidence of extrahepatic biliary atresia.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice.

Question: Which of the following instructions should be given to a lactating mother regarding drug usage?
Choices:
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk
  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should be careful about the medications they take.
  Some drugs can be secreted in milk and can harm the baby.
  Therefore, they should be advised on how to take medications.
  Option A is incorrect because drugs can be secreted in milk.
  Option B is incorrect because drugs with longer half-life means these will remain in the body for a more extended period and thus will be secreted in milk for longer periods.
  Option C is correct because it can reduce the concentration of drugs in the milk by delaying secretion.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before the next dose.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Drugs can be secreted into the breast milk and can cause harm to the baby.
  Therefore, nursing mothers must be very careful with drug usage while lactating.
  The safest approach is to avoid drug usage if possible. 
  If drug use is necessary, then the lowest effective dose should be used.
  Drugs with longer half-life or those that are metabolized into active compounds only in the liver should be avoided.
  The mother should not stop breastfeeding or pump and dump, but instead feed her baby just before a dose to avoid the peak drug concentration in the milk.
  Therefore, the correct answer is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose.

Question: A 70 years old hypeensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease was diagnosed recently with Type 2 diabetes mellitus. He doesn't want to take injectable insulin. Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The patient is 70 years old and has stage 5 Chronic Kidney Disease (CKD), which indicates significantly reduced kidney function.
  CKD requires renal dose modification of most drugs, including oral hypoglycemic agents, to avoid toxicity.
  Type 2 diabetes mellitus requires treatment with medications like oral hypoglycemic agents, avoiding insulin injection is patient choice.
  The preferred medication should be the one that does not require renal dose modification.
  Among the choices, Linagliptin and Vildagliptin are Dipeptidyl peptidase-4 (DPP-4) inhibitors and are not primarily excreted by the kidneys.
  Glimepiride and Repaglinide are Sulfonylureas and Meglitinides, respectively, and both are excreted by the kidneys and require dose adjustments in renal insufficiency.
  Therefore, the preferred option in this patient will be A: Linagliptin or C: Vildagliptin.
Action: Answer("A or C")

- The patient has chronic kidney disease, so renal dose adjustment is required for many drugs.
- We need to choose an oral hypoglycemic agent that does not require renal dose adjustment.
- Linagliptin, Vildagliptin, and Repaglinide are partially renally excreted, thus require renal dosing adjustments.
- Glimepiride is primarily metabolized by the liver, and no renal dosage adjustment is necessary.
- Glimepiride may cause hypoglycemia in the elderly, so it should be used with caution.
- Therefore, Glimepiride is the best choice for this patient.

  A: 16 lp
  B: 22 lp
  C: 30 lp
  D: 10 lp

  The resolution of an IOPA radiograph is usually around 20 lp.
  The closest value to 20 lp in the given choices is 22 lp, which is also a common resolution used for dental radiographs.

- Systematic random sampling: A sampling method where the sample is selected systematically.
- Simple random sampling: A sampling method where each element has an equal chance of being selected.
- Stratified random sampling: Separating the population into strata and then taking samples from each stratum.
- Cluster sampling: Dividing the population into clusters and then selecting random clusters for the sample.
- We need to select patients based on particular potential factors, which means we need to separate the population based on these factors. Hence, option C: Stratified random sampling is the correct answer.
Action: Answer("C")

- Simple random sampling: Each member of the population has an equal chance of being included in the sample.
- Stratified random sampling: Population is divided into subgroups (strata) and samples are taken from each subgroup.
- Cluster sampling: Clusters or groups are randomly selected, and all individuals in each selected cluster are included in the sample.

Question: Which of the following has strong familial inheritance:
Choices:
  A: Functional class III
  B: Class I type I
  C: Class II div I
  D: Class II div II
Response 0:
Thought:
  Familial inheritance refers to a condition or trait that runs in families through genes.
  Functional Class III refers to malocclusion where the lower jaw is more prominent than the upper jaw.
  Class I type I refers to ideal occlusion with normal jaw and teeth alignment.
  Class II div I and Class II div II both refer to malocclusion where the upper teeth and jaw overlap the lower teeth and jaw.
  Strong familial inheritance is commonly seen in Class II malocclusions.
  Therefore, the answer is either C or D.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
    In dentistry, the Angle's classification of malocclusion is used to describe types of occlusion (how teeth come together). 
    Class I (neutroclusion) is the "ideal" occlusion where the first molars are aligned and the upper incisor is slightly over the lower incisors.
    Class II (distocclusion) is when the lower first molar is posterior to the upper first molar. 
    Class III (mesiocclusion) is when the lower first molar is anterior to the upper first molar. 
    Class II malocclusion have a strong familial inheritance.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Dental classification is a way to describe the occlusion relationship between the maxillary and mandibular arches.
  Class I is normal occlusion, class II is overbite due to retrognathism or prognathism, and class III is underbite due to prognathism.
  Family inheritance plays a role in the development of malocclusion in certain individuals.
  Class III, which is prognathism or underbite, is known to have the strongest familial inheritance.
  So, the answer is A: Functional class III.

  Class II div I malocclusion is characterized by a retrognathic mandible, a Class II molar and canine relationship, a deep overbite, and typically a convex profile.

  Tympanic membrane is not composed of collagen, but it is composed of three layers: outer epithelial layer, middle fibrous layer, and inner mucosal layer.
  Diaphragm is a dome-shaped muscular and tendon partition separating the thoracic and abdominal cavities in mammals that plays a major role in breathing.
  The cornea is the outermost transparent layer of the eye consisting of stroma, Bowman's layer, and Descemet's membrane.
  Bowman's layer is composed of randomly arranged collagen fibrils, whereas Descemet's membrane is composed of type IV collagen and other non-collagenous proteins.
  Therefore, the answer is not A, C, or D.
  The answer is B, the cornea.

Choices:

  B: Pancuronium
  C: Mivacurum
  D: Decamethonium

  Short-acting non-depolarising muscle relaxants are useful when intubation is required for a short time or when muscle relaxation is needed for the shortest possible time.
  Succinylcholine is a depolarising muscle relaxant, and the other three are non-depolarising muscle relaxants.
  Pancuronium and Decamethonium are long-acting while Mivacurium is intermediate-acting.
